The commentary: 'Ascending to the highest' and it is called the genus of genera, and the species (may be ordered) 'descending to the lowest' and it is called the species of species, and what is between them are intermediates. The third: the differentia, which is predicated of a thing in answer to 'what thing is it in its essence?', for it distinguishes it from the things that share in the proximate genus, [and it is] a part in the external. His saying 'ascending': that is, the ascent is from the specific to the general, and that is because the genus of the genus is more general than the genus, and so on until a genus that has no genus above it, which is the highest, and the genus of genera is like substance. His saying 'descending': that is, the descent is from the general to the specific, and that is because the species of the species is more specific than the species, and so on until a species that has no species under it, which is the lowest, and the species of species is like human. His saying 'and what is between them are intermediates': that is, what is between the highest and the lowest in the two chains of species and genera is called intermediates. So what is between the highest genus and the lowest genus are intermediate genera, and what is between the highest species and the lowest species are intermediate species. This is if the pronoun refers merely to the highest and lowest. But if it refers to the highest genus and the lowest species mentioned explicitly, then the meaning is: that what is between the highest genus and the lowest species are intermediates: either a genus only, like the highest species; or a species only, like the lowest genus; or both a genus and a species together, like the growing body. Then know that the author (al-musannif) did not address the individual genus and the individual species, perhaps because the discussion is about what is ordered, and the individual is not included in the chain of ordering, or because of uncertainty of their existence. His saying 'what thing': know that the word 'ayy' is placed to request that which distinguishes the thing. (He) says 'and it is predicated...' i.e., the universal predicated, for the divider is considered in all the divisions; the universal is like a genus that includes the five universals, and by his saying 'predicated of a thing in answer to 'what thing' is excluded the species and the genus, because they are not said in answer to 'what thing' but rather in answer to 'what is it (mahiyyah)?' as previously, and also the universal accident.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the definitions of the ascending and descending chains and on the differentia (الفصل). The commentator explains the terms: 'ascending to the highest' means going from specific to general, resulting in the genus of genera (جنس الأجناس), exemplified by substance. 'Descending to the lowest' means going from general to specific, resulting in the species of species (نوع الأنواع), exemplified by human. What lies between these extremes are called intermediates, which can be intermediate genera or species. The commentator then analyzes a nuance: if the pronoun 'between them' refers to the highest and lowest generally, then intermediates separate the chains of genera and species; if it refers specifically to the highest genus and lowest species, then the intermediate can be either a genus only, a species only, or both (like the growing body). Next, he notes that the author (المصنف) did not mention the 'individual genus' (جنس مفرد) and 'individual species' (نوع مفرد) because they are not part of the ordered chain or their existence is uncertain. Finally, he clarifies the definition of the differentia: it is a universal predicate that answers 'what thing is it in its essence?' and distinguishes the thing from others sharing the same proximate genus; it is an external part. He contrasts this with genus and species, which answer 'what is it?' (ماهو), and with universal accident. This lesson is crucial for understanding how the five universals are hierarchically arranged.

نوع الأنواع
فصل

The differentia is a universal that answers 'what thing in its essence?' and is an external part of the definition, distinct from genus and species which answer 'what is it?'.

Hierarchy of Genera and Species
Author explains hierarchy of genera and species

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the highest genus (jins al-ajnas) and lowest species (naw' al-anwa') in a classification, and trace the ascending and descending series with examples from Islamic logic.

Core Idea
The genus-of-genera is the most universal; the species-of-species is the most specific.

In Islamic logic, genera and species are arranged in ordered hierarchies. This passage clarifies the two directions of that hierarchy: ascending from specific to general, culminating in the highest genus (jins al-ajnas), and descending from general to specific, ending at the lowest species (naw' al-anwa'). Understanding this structure is essential for correct definition and classification in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ascending series
Notice that 'ascending' means moving from a specific concept to a more general one. For example, human (specific) → animal (more general) → body (even more general) → substance (most general). The endpoint is jins al-ajnas, which has no genus above it, like substance (jawhar).
Think of it like a ladder: each step up broadens the category.
2
Identify the descending series
The descending series moves from general to specific. From substance down to human, each step narrows the category. The endpoint is naw' al-anwa', which has no species below it, like human (insan).
This is the opposite direction: from broadest to narrowest.
3
Understand intermediate terms
Between the highest and lowest, there are intermediate genera and species. For instance, if the highest genus is substance and the lowest species is human, then animal is an intermediate genus (it is a species relative to substance, but a genus relative to human).
Intermediates can be genera, species, or both, depending on perspective.
4
Note the omission of single genus/species
The author did not discuss 'single genus' (al-jins al-mufrad) or 'single species' (al-naw' al-mufrad), which are terms that do not fit into an ordered chain. Their existence is uncertain or they are outside the scope of this discussion.
This shows that the hierarchy is the primary concern in definition theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متصاعدة الى العالى ويسمى جنس الاجناس والانواع متنازلة الى السافل و يسمى نوع الانواع و ما بينهما متوسطات. قوله «متصاعدة»: بان يكون الترقى من خاص الى عام وذلك لان جنس الجنس يكون اعم من الجنس و هكذا الى جنس الذي لا جنس له فوقه و هو العالى و جنس الاجناس كالجوهر. قوله «متنازلة» بان يكون التنزل من عام الى خاص وذلك لان نوع النوع يكون اخص من النوع وهكذا الا ان الى نوع لا نوع تحته و هو السافل ونوع الانواع كالانسان. قوله و ما بينها متوسطات» اى ما بين العالى والسافل في سلسلتي الانواع والاجناس يسمى متوسطات فما بين الجنس العالى و الجنس السافل اجناس متوسطة وما بين النوع العالى و النوع السافل انواع متوسطة هذا ان رجع الضمير الى مجرد العالى والسافل و ان عاد الى الجنس العالى و النوع السافل المذكورين صريحاً كان المعنى : ان ما بين الجنس العالى والنوع السافل متوسطات: اما جنس متوسط فقط كالنوع العالى او نوع متوسط فقط كالجنس السافل او جنس متوسط و نوع متوسط معاً كالجسم النامي. ثم اعلم ان المصنف لم يتعرض للجنس المفرد والنوع المفرد اما لان الكلام فيما يترتب والمفرد ليس داخلاً في سلسلة الترتيب و اما لعدم تيقن وجودهما.
Ascending to the highest is called the genus of genera and species descending to the lowest is called the species of species, and what is between them are intermediates. His statement: 'ascending': meaning the ascent is from specific to general, because the genus of a genus is more general than the genus, and so on until a genus that has no genus above it, which is the highest and the genus of genera, like substance. His statement: 'descending': meaning the descent is from general to specific, because the species of a species is more specific than the species, and so on until a species that has no species below it, which is the lowest and the species of species, like human. His statement: 'and what is between them are intermediates': meaning what is between the highest and the lowest in the two chains of species and genera is called intermediates. So between the highest genus and the lowest genus are intermediate genera, and between the highest species and the lowest species are intermediate species. This if the pronoun refers to merely the highest and lowest; and if it refers to the highest genus and the lowest species explicitly mentioned, the meaning would be that what is between the highest genus and the lowest species are intermediates: either a genus only (like the highest species), or a species only (like the lowest genus), or both a genus and a species together (like the growing body). Then know that the author did not address the single genus and single species, either because the discussion is about what is ordered and the single is not included in the series of ordering, or due to uncertainty of their existence.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion of the concepts of 'ascending' and 'descending' series in the hierarchy of genera and species. The author explains that the ascending series goes from the specific to the general, culminating in the highest genus (jins al-ajnas, e.g., substance). Conversely, the descending series goes from the general to the specific, ending with the lowest species (naw' al-anwa', e.g., human). The term 'intermediates' (mutawassitat) is then clarified: it can refer to either genera or species that lie between the highest and lowest. The author also notes that the original author did not discuss 'single genus' and 'single species' because either they are not part of an ordered series or their existence is uncertain.

نوع الأنواع

The hierarchy of genera and species has two extremes: the highest genus (jins al-ajnas) and the lowest species (naw' al-anwa'), with intermediates in between.

10 min
Defining Fasl and the Interrogative 'Ayyu Shay'
Author defines fasl and clarifies the technical usage of 'ayyu shay'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the essential differentia (fasl) in a definition and explain why the interrogative 'ayyu shay' is used to seek it.

Core Idea
The differentia answers 'which thing?' after the genus is known, not 'what is it?'.

The third universal is the differentia (fasl), which distinguishes a species from others sharing the same proximate genus. Logicians define it using the interrogative 'ayyu shay' (which thing?) to signal that the differentia is sought after the genus is known. Understanding this technical shift is essential for correct definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of fasl
Locate the Arabic sentence starting 'الثالث: الفصل...'. The definition states: 'what is said of a thing in answer to which thing is it in its essence?'
2
Understand the role of 'ayyu shay'
The word 'ayyu' is linguistically general, seeking any distinguisher. Logicians restricted it to seek only the differentia, not the genus or complete definition.
Example: seeing a figure and asking 'which animal?' yields the species (e.g. human), not the genus.
3
Distinguish fasl from hadd tamm
If asked 'which thing?', one could answer with the complete definition (e.g. 'rational animal'), so logicians restricted 'ayyu' to exclude such answers.
This leads to al-Razi's objection, which is addressed in the next lesson.

الثالث: الفصل و هو المقول على الشيء في جواب اى شيء هو فى ذاته فان ميزه عن المشاركات فى الجنس القريب جزء في الخارج. قوله ای شیء» اعلم ان كلمة «اى» موضوعة ليطلب بها ما يميز الشئ فقريب أو البعيد فبعيد يشاركه فما اضيف اليه هذه الكلمة. مثلاً اذا ابصرت شبحاً عن بعيد و ايقنت انه حيوان لكن ترددت فى انه هل هو انسان او فرس او غيرهما ؟ تقول اى حيوان هذا ؟ فيجاب بما يخصصه ويميزه عن مشاركاته فى الحيوانية. اذا عرفت هذا فنقول : اذا قلنا الانسان اى شيء هو فى ذاته» كان المطلوب ذاتياً من ذاتيات الانسان يميزه عما يشاركه فى الشيئية فيصح ان يجاب بانه حيوان ناطق كما صح ان يجاب بانه ناطق فيلزم صحة وقوع الحد في جواب اى شيء هو فى ذاته و ايضاً يلزم ان لا يكون تعريف الفصل مانعاً الغيره الصدقه على الحد التام و هذا مما استشكله الامام الرازي فى هذا المقام و اجاب عنه صاحب المحاكمات بان معنى اى و ان كانت بحسب وضع اللغة لطلب المميز مطلقا لكن ارباب المعقول اصطلحوا على انه لطلب مميز لا يكون مقولا فى جواب ما هو. وبهذا يخرج الحد والجنس ايضا . و للمحقق الطوسی رحمة الله تعالى عليه هيهنا مسلك آخر ادق و اتقن و هو انا لأنسأل عن الفصل الا بعد ان نعلم ان للشيء جنساً بناء على ان ما لا جنس له لا فصل له و اذا علمنا الشيء بالجنس فنطلب ما يميزه عن المشاركات في ذلك الجنس فنقول : الانسان اى شيء هو فى ذاته فتعين الجواب بانه ناطق لا غير فكلمة «شيء» فى التعريف كناية عن الجنس المعلوم الذي يطلب ما يميز الشيء عن مشاركاته في ذلك الجنس فحينئذ يندفع الاشكال بحذافيره. قوله «فقريب» كالناطق بالنسبة الى الانسان حيث يميزه عن جميع المشاركات فى جنسه القريب و هو الحيوان. قوله «فبعيد»: كالحساس بالنسبة الى الانسان حيث يميزه عن المشاركات لانه لا يقال في الجواب اصلاً على ما هو التحقيق وسيأتى و خرج بقوله فى ذاته الخاصة، لانها انما يقال في جواب اى شيء هو فى «عرضه» و كذا العرض العام لو قلنا بجواز وقوعه في الجواب. ثم الفصل في اللغة: القطع ، يقال : فصلته فانفصل اى قطعته فانقطع، ثم استعمل بمعنى ما تميز به شيء عن شيء لازماً كان او مفارقاً ذاتياً او عرضياً استعمالاً للمصدر بمعنى الفاعل كالعدل بمعنى العادل، ثم نقله المنطقيون الى الذاتى المتميز به الشيء عن الآخر استعمالاً للمطلق في المقيد.
The third: the differentia, and it is what is said of a thing in answer to 'a thing, what is it in its essence' such that it distinguishes it from sharers in the proximate genus, being a part in the external existence. His statement: 'a thing' – know that the word 'ayyu' is placed to seek what distinguishes the thing, so the near is near and the far is far, sharing with it what is added to this word. For example, if you see a figure from afar and you are certain it is an animal but you are uncertain whether it is a human, a horse, or something else, you say: 'Which animal is this?' and it is answered with what specifies it and distinguishes it from sharers in animality. When you know this, we say: when we say 'human, what is it in its essence', what is sought is an essential from among the essentials of human that distinguishes it from what shares with it in thingness, so it is valid to answer with 'rational animal' just as it is valid to answer with 'rational'. Thus it necessarily follows that the definition (hadd) can validly occur in answer to 'what is it in its essence', and also it necessarily follows that the definition of differentia does not prevent its being true of the complete limit (hadd tam). This is an objection raised by al-Imam al-Razi in this context, and the author of al-Muhakamat answered that the meaning of 'ayyu' – even if according to linguistic usage it is for seeking a distinguisher absolutely – nevertheless the scholars of intellectual matters have agreed that it is for seeking a distinguisher that is not said in answer to 'what is it'. By this, the definition (hadd) and genus are excluded. And al-Muhaqqiq al-Tusi (may Allah have mercy on him) has another approach here, more subtle and more accurate: we do not ask about the differentia except after we know that the thing has a genus, based on the principle that what has no genus has no differentia. And when we know the thing by its genus, we seek what distinguishes it from sharers in that genus, so we say: 'human, what is it in its essence', and the answer is determined as 'rational' only. So the word 'thing' in the definition is a metaphor for the known genus whose distinguisher is sought. Then the objection is completely refuted. His statement: 'near', like 'rational' with respect to human, as it distinguishes from all sharers in its proximate genus, which is animal. His statement: 'far', like 'sensitive' with respect to human, for it distinguishes from sharers because it is not said in the answer at all according to the verification, and it will come later. And by his statement 'in its essence' the special (khassa) is excluded, for it is only said in answer to 'what is it in its accident', and likewise the general accident if we allow its occurrence in answer. Then the differentia in language means cutting; it is said 'fasaltuhu fa infasala' i.e. I cut it so it became cut. Then it was used to mean what distinguishes a thing from another, whether necessary or accidental, essential or accidental, using the verbal noun in the sense of the active participle like 'justice' in the sense of 'just'. Then logicians transferred it to the essential by which a thing is distinguished from another, using the absolute for the restricted.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage defines the third universal, the differentia (fasl), and clarifies the technical meaning of the interrogative phrase 'ayyu shay'' (which thing?) in its definition. The definition states: fasl is what is said of a thing in answer to 'ayyu shay' huwa fi dhatih' (which thing is it in its essence?) and distinguishes it from others sharing the proximate genus, and it is a part in external existence. The commentator first explains that the word 'ayyu' is used linguistically to seek a distinguisher, giving the example of seeing a figure from afar and asking 'which animal is this?' to get a specific answer like 'human'. However, an objection arises: if we ask 'human, which thing is it in its essence?', we might answer with the complete definition (hadd tam) 'rational animal' or simply the differentia 'rational'. This would mean the complete definition falls under the same interrogative, making the definition of fasl not exclusive. Al-Imam al-Razi raised this objection. The author of al-Muhakamat responded that logicians have restricted 'ayyu' to seek a distinguisher that is not said in answer to 'what is it?' (ma huwa), thus excluding the complete definition and genus. Al-Muhaqqiq al-Tusi gave a more precise solution: we only ask for the differentia after knowing the genus, because something without a genus has no differentia. So when we know the genus (e.g., animal for human), we ask 'which thing is it?' with 'thing' referring implicitly to that known genus, seeking the specific differentia (e.g., rational). This blocks the objection entirely. The passage then clarifies 'near' (qarib) and 'far' (ba'id) differentia with examples: 'rational' for human is near, distinguishing from all that share the proximate genus (animal); 'sensitive' (hassas) is far because it is not a differentia in the strict sense. Finally, the etymology of 'fasl' is given: it originally means 'cutting', then used for any distinguishing feature (accidental or essential), and finally restricted by logicians to the essential differentia.

D) To test if the figure is an animal

Key Takeaway
The differentia is the essential feature that distinguishes a species within its genus, and the interrogative 'ayyu shay' is technically restricted to seek it alone.

?
Given the definition of prayer (صلاة) as 'specific sayings and actions, beginning with takbir and ending with taslim', identify the genus and the differentia. Explain why the differentia is 'near' (qarib) rather than 'far' (ba'id).

Resolving the Objection: Al-Tusi's Refined Solution
Author presents al-Razi's objection and two solutions, emphasizing al-Tusi's refined approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct al-Razi's objection to the definition of fasl and explain al-Tusi's solution that the word 'thing' in the definition refers to the known genus.

Core Idea
Al-Tusi solved the puzzle by realizing 'thing' in the definition silently points to the already-known genus.

Al-Razi objected that the definition of fasl would also include the complete definition. The author of al-Muhakamat responded by pointing to the technical agreement that 'ayyu' seeks only what is not said in answer to 'what is it?'. But al-Tusi gave a more subtle solution: we only ask for the differentia after knowing the genus, so the word 'thing' in 'which thing?' implicitly refers to that known genus, ensuring the answer is only the differentia.

Guided Path
1
Restate al-Razi's objection
The objection is that the definition of fasl does not exclude the complete definition (hadd tam), because both can answer 'which thing?'.
2
Understand al-Muhakamat's response
The response states that logicians have agreed that 'ayyu' in this context seeks a distinguisher that is not said in answer to 'what is it?', thus excluding the complete definition and genus.
This is a social convention, not a logical necessity.
3
Analyze al-Tusi's solution
Al-Tusi argues that we ask for the differentia only after knowing the genus. So the word 'thing' in 'which thing?' is a metaphor for the known genus. The answer is determined as the differentia only.
This completely removes the objection because the complete definition would include the genus, which is already known and not sought.

Commentary

The definition states: fasl is what is said of a thing in answer to 'ayyu shay' huwa fi dhatih' (which thing is it in its essence?) and distinguishes it from others sharing the proximate genus, and it is a part in external existence. The Differentia in Answer to 'What Is It in Itself' and Resolution of Objections
Author examines whether fasl answers 'ayy shay' huwa fi dhatihi', presents objections and answers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the differentia can answer 'What is it in itself?' according to al-Tusi's method, and identify the role of the genus in the question.

Core Idea
The differentia answers 'What is it?' only after the genus is known; the question implies the genus.

This passage tackles a subtle point in definition: can the differentia alone be a sufficient answer to the question 'What is it in itself?' The logicians, led by Imam al-Razi, raised an objection against this possibility, and al-Tusi provided a refined resolution that remains a landmark in Islamic logic. Understanding this debate sharpens your grasp of the five universals and how definitions function.

Guided Path
1
Locate the problem
Identify why al-Razi thought the differentia alone cannot answer 'What is it in itself?' because the complete definition (hadd) also answers it, so the differentia would not be exclusive.
The objection hinges on the overlap of answers.
2
Examine al-Muhakamat's response
Understand the terminological distinction: in logic, 'ayy' demands a differentiator not said in answer to 'ma huwa', so the definition and genus are excluded.
This is a stipulative solution.
3
Analyze al-Tusi's alternative
Recognize that the question 'ayy shay' huwa fi dhatihi' uses 'shay'' as a metonym for the known genus, so the answer is only the differentia.
Al-Tusi's method is grounded in the logical priority of genus.
4
Distinguish close and distant differentia
Apply the distinction between immediate (close) and remote (distant) differentiators, and see why only the close one is given in answer.
E.g., 'rational' is close; 'sensitive' is distant for human.

في الكليات الخمس فقريب أو البعيد فبعيد يشاركه فما اضيف اليه هذه الكلمة. مثلاً اذا ابصرت شبحاً عن بعيد و ايقنت انه حيوان لكن ترددت فى انه هل هو انسان او فرس او غيرهما؟ تقول اى حيوان هذا؟ فيجاب بما يخصصه ويميزه عن مشاركاته فى الحيوانية. اذا عرفت هذا فنقول: اذا قلنا الانسان اى شيء هو فى ذاته كان المطلوب ذاتياً من ذاتيات الانسان يميزه عما يشاركه فى الشيئية فيصح ان يجاب بانه حيوان ناطق كما صح ان يجاب بانه ناطق فيلزم صحة وقوع الحد في جواب اى شيء هو فى ذاته و ايضاً يلزم ان لا يكون تعريف الفصل مانعاً الغيره الصدقه على الحد التام و هذا مما استشكله الامام الرازي فى هذا المقام و اجاب عنه صاحب المحاكمات بان معنى اى و ان كانت بحسب وضع اللغة لطلب المميز مطلقا لكن ارباب المعقول اصطلحوا على انه لطلب مميز لا يكون مقولا فى جواب ما هو. وبهذا يخرج الحد والجنس ايضا. و للمحقق الطوسی رحمة الله تعالى عليه هيهنا مسلك آخر ادق و اتقن و هو انا لأنسأل عن الفصل الا بعد ان نعلم ان للشيء جنساً بناء على ان ما لا جنس له لا فصل له و اذا علمنا الشيء بالجنس فنطلب ما يميزه عن المشاركات في ذلك الجنس فنقول: الانسان اى شيء هو فى ذاته فتعين الجواب بانه ناطق لا غير فكلمة «شيء» فى التعريف كناية عن الجنس المعلوم الذي يطلب ما يميز الشيء عن مشاركاته في ذلك الجنس فحينئذ يندفع الاشكال بحذا فيره قوله «فقريب» كالناطق بالنسبة الى الانسان حيث يميزه عن جميع المشاركات فى جنسه القريب و هو الحيوان. قوله «فبعيد»: كالحساس بالنسبة الى الانسان حيث يميزه عن المشاركات لانه لا يقال في الجواب اصلاً على ما هو التحقيق وسيأتى و خرج بقوله فى ذاته الخاصة، لانها انما يقال في جواب اى شيء هو فى «عرضه» و كذا العرض العام لو قلنا بجواز وقوعه في الجواب.
On the five universals: the close (differentia) or the distant (differentia) so distant. It shares with it what is added to this word. For example, when you see a silhouette from afar and you are certain it is an animal, but you are uncertain whether it is a human, a horse, or something else, you say: 'Any animal is this?' So it is answered with what specifies it and distinguishes it from its participants in animality. When you know this, we say: When we say 'Human: what is it in itself?' the required is an essential from the essentials of the human that distinguishes it from what shares it in 'thingness'. So it is correct that it is answered with 'rational animal', just as it is correct that it is answered with 'rational'. Thus it follows that the definition (hadd) occurs in the answer to 'what is it in itself', and also it follows that the definition of the differentia (fasl) does not exclude its being true of the complete definition. This is what Imam al-Razi objected to in this context. The author of al-Muhakamat answered that the meaning of 'ayy' even if according to the convention of language is to demand the differentiator absolutely, yet the people of rational sciences have stipulated that it demands a differentiator that is not said in answer to 'what is it' (ma huwa). By this, the definition and the genus are excluded. And al-Muhaqqiq al-Tusi—may God have mercy on him—has here another path, more subtle and more precise: that we only ask about the differentia after we know that the thing has a genus, based on the fact that whatever has no genus has no differentia. When we know the thing by its genus, we ask for what distinguishes it from the participants in that genus. So we say: 'Human: what is it in itself?' Then the answer is determined to be 'rational' and nothing else. So the word 'thing' in the definition is a metonym for the known genus, by which is sought what distinguishes the thing from its participants in that genus. Thus the objection is repelled completely. His saying 'close' like 'rational' in relation to the human, where it distinguishes it from all participants in its close genus, which is animal. His saying 'distant' like 'sensitive' in relation to the human, where it distinguishes it from participants because it is not said in the answer at all, as is the verification and will come later. And he excluded by his saying 'in itself' the special, because they are said only in answer to 'what is it in its accident' and likewise the general accident if we allow its occurrence in the answer.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage defines the role of the differentia (fasl) in answering the question 'What is it in itself?' It begins with an illustrative example: seeing a distant shape known to be an animal but not knowing which species, we ask 'Any animal is this?' and the answer specifies. This mirrors the logical analysis: when we ask of a human 'What is it in itself?', we seek an essential differentiator from all other things. The author notes that both 'rational animal' (the complete definition) and 'rational' (the differentia alone) could be given as answers, leading to a problem: the definition (hadd) would then be a valid answer to 'ayy shay' huwa fi dhatihi', and the definition of fasl would not exclude it. Imam al-Razi raised this objection. The response from Sahib al-Muhakamat is that 'ayy' in logical terminology seeks a differentiator that is not said in response to 'ma huwa', thus excluding the definition and genus. Then al-Muhaqqiq al-Tusi gives a superior method: we ask about the fasl only after knowing the genus, so in 'What is it in itself?' the word 'shay'' stands for the known genus, and the answer is only the differentia. This resolves the issue. Finally, the passage distinguishes 'close' differentia (e.g., 'rational' for human, distinguishing from all in the immediate genus 'animal') and 'distant' (e.g., 'sensitive' distinguishing from all in the remote genus 'growing body'), with the note that the latter is not given in answer.

Key Terms
الفصل (al-fasl): The differentia; an essential (dhati) attribute that distinguishes a species from other species sharing the same genus. [Note: No significant shift; stable across the tradition.]
أي شيء هو في ذاته (ayy shay' huwa fi dhatihi): The question 'What is it in itself?' seeking the essential nature of a thing, answered by genus and differentia or by differentia alone in al-Tusi's view. [Note: Considered interchangeable with 'ma huwa' in some texts; here nuanced to avoid including complete definition.]
الحد (al-hadd): The complete definition, consisting of genus and differentia, which fully defines a species. [Note: No significant shift.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Muhaqqiq al-Tusi's method, why does the differentia alone answer 'What is it in itself?' for a human?
A) Because the differentia includes the genus implicitly.
B) Because the word 'shay'' in the question refers to the already known genus, so the answer gives only the differentiator.
C) Because the question is about the accident, not essence.
D) Because the differentia is the only essential part.

Key Takeaway
The differentia can answer 'What is it in itself?' only when the genus is already known, and the question's word 'thing' implicitly refers to that genus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given the definition of 'zakat' as 'a specific portion of wealth given to specified recipients under conditions', identify which part is the genus (wealth given) and which is the differentia (specific portion, recipients, conditions), and explain how the differentia answers 'What is it in itself?' after the genus is known.
?
Al-Tusi's method requires that the genus be known before asking for the differentia. In the context of defining 'sawm' (fasting) as 'abstaining from specific acts from dawn to sunset', what is the genus (abstention), and how does the differentia 'from specific acts from dawn to sunset' distinguish it from other forms of abstention?

The Linguistic and Technical Meaning of Fasl (Differentia)
Author defines fasl linguistically and technically.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the semantic shift of 'fasl' from its linguistic meaning to its technical logical usage, and identify the essential condition for a differentia in logic.

Core Idea
Fasl moved from 'cutting' to 'distinguishing' to the essential differentiator of a species.

The differentia (fasl) is a fundamental tool in definition. But where does this term come from, and how did it acquire its precise logical meaning? This lesson unpacks the linguistic origin of 'fasl' and the critical transfer that logicians made to restrict it to essential differentiators.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic root
The word 'fasl' literally means cutting. The author gives the verb form 'fasaltuhu fa infasala' meaning 'I cut it so it was cut'. This concrete origin is the starting point.
2
Track the broadening of meaning
Before the logicians, 'fasl' was used for any distinguishing mark, whether essential or accidental. The passage says it was used for 'that by which a thing is distinguished from another thing, whether inseparable or separable, essential or accidental'.
3
Recognise the logicians' restriction
The logicians transferred the term to 'the essential by which the thing is distinguished from the other'. They used the absolute for the restricted, narrowing the meaning to essential distinctions only.
4
Connect to the five universals
This essential differentiator is one of the five universals, critical for constructing definitions (hadd). It is the differentia that, combined with genus, gives the species.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الفصل في اللغة: القطع ، يقال : فصلته فانفصل اى قطعته فانقطع، ثم استعمل بمعنى ما تميز به شيء عن شيء لازماً كان او مفارقاً ذاتياً او عرضياً استعمالاً للمصدر بمعنى الفاعل كالعدل بمعنى العادل، ثم نقله المنطقيون الى الذاتى المتميز به الشيء عن الآخر استعمالاً للمطلق في المقيد. و اذا نسب الى ما يميزه فيقوم و الى ما يميزه عنه والمقوم للعالى مقوم السافل الحاشية قوله واذ انسب: الفصل له نسبة الى الماهية التي هو فصل مميز لها ونسبة الى الجنس الذي يميز الماهية عنه من بين افراده فهو بالاعتبار الاول يسمى مقوماً لأنه جزء للماهية و محصل لها و بالاعتبار الثاني يسمى مقسماً لانه بانضمامه الى هذا الجنس وجوداً يحصل قسماً وعدماً يحصل قسما آخر كما ترى في تقسيم الحيوان الى الحيوان الناطق و الحيوان الغير الناطق. قوله « والمقوم للعالى» اللام للاستغراق ای کل فصل مقوم للعالى فهو فصل مقوم للسافل لان مقوم العالى جزء العالى والعالى جزء للسافل وجزء الجزء جزء فتقوم العالى جزء للسافل . ثم انه يميز السافل عن كل ما يميز العالى عنه فيكون جزء مميزاً له و هو معنى المقوم. وليعلم ان المراد بالعالى هيهنا كل جنس او نوع يكون فوق آخر سواء كان فوقه آخر او لم يكن وكذا المراد بالسافل كل جنس او نوع يكون تحت آخر سواء كان تحته آخر او لم يكن حتى ان الجنس المتوسط عال بالنسبة الى ما تحته وسافل بالنسبة الى ما فوقه . قوله واذا انسب: اى الفصل الى النوع الذي يميزه عن الانواع المشتركة معه فى جنس، فالفصل من هذه الناحية يقال له: «مقوم» لأنه جزء ذاتى للنوع و الجزء من مقومات ماتركب منه . و اذا وأ نسب الى الجنس الذي ميز عن سائر انواعه نوعاً بخصوصه فالفصل بهذا الاعتبار يقال له: «مقسم» لانه قسم الجنس الى قسم فيه هذا الفصل والفارق و قسم ليس فيه هذا الفصل والفارق، مثلاً الناطق اذا نسب الى الانسان فهو مقوم له ، لانه ذاتى من ذاتياته واذا نسب الى الحيوان الذي ميز عن سائر انواعه هذا النوع المخصوص وهو الانسان فهو مقسم له الى حيوان ناطق و هو الانسان وحيوان غير ناطق وهو غير الانسان. قال والمقوم للعالى: كالنامي المقوم للجسم النامي الذي هو الشجر وغيره من كل جسم له نمو، مقوم للسافل الذى هو الحيوان و الانسان ايضاً، فان الحيوان والانسان مما يشتركان في الجسم مع غيرهما من الاجسام فاذا تميز الجسم النامي عن غيره من انواع الاجسام بالنامي فقد تميز الحيوان والانسان ايضاً عن سائر انواع الاجسام بانهما ناميان لان الجسم النامي جزء من الحيوان و من الانسان، فالميزة التي تكون نصيبه نصيب ما تركب منه ايضاً و من جملة ما تركب منه الحيوان والانسان.
Then fasl in language: cutting. It is said: 'fasaltuhu fa infasala' meaning I cut it, so it was cut. Then it was used in the sense of that by which a thing is distinguished from another thing, whether it is inseparable or separable, essential or accidental, using the infinitive in the sense of the active participle, like 'adl' in the sense of 'adil'. Then the logicians transferred it to the essential by which the thing is distinguished from the other, using the absolute for the restricted. And when it is related to what it distinguishes, it constitutes; and to what it distinguishes from, it divides. And the constituent (muqawwim) of the higher is a constituent of the lower. The marginal note: his saying 'when related': the differentia has a relation to the quiddity for which it is a distinguishing differentia, and a relation to the genus from which it distinguishes the quiddity among its individuals. So by the first consideration it is called 'muqawwim' because it is a part of the quiddity and its concretizer, and by the second consideration it is called 'muqassim' because by its conjunction with this genus, existentially, a division results, and by its absence another division results, as you see in the division of animal into rational animal and non-rational animal. His saying 'and the muqawwim of the higher'—the lam is for generality: every differentia that is a constituent of the higher is a constituent of the lower, because the constituent of the higher is a part of the higher, and the higher is a part of the lower, and a part of a part is a part; so the constituent of the higher is a part of the lower. Then it distinguishes the lower from everything from which it distinguishes the higher, thus it is a distinguishing part of it, and that is the meaning of muqawwim. Let it be known that by 'higher' here is meant every genus or species that is above another, whether or not there is another above it; similarly, by 'lower' is meant every genus or species that is under another, whether or not there is another under it, so that the intermediate genus is higher relative to what is under it and lower relative to what is above it. His saying 'when related': that is, the differentia to the species that it distinguishes from the species sharing the same genus; so from this aspect it is called 'muqawwim' because it is an essential part of the species, and the part is among the constituents of what it is composed of. And when it is related to the genus from which it distinguishes a specific species, then the differentia by this consideration is called 'muqassim' because it divides the genus into a division that has this differentia and distinction, and a division that does not have this differentia and distinction. For example, 'rational' when related to human is a constituent of it, because it is among its essentials; and when related to animal, which distinguishes this specific species (human) from its other species, it is a divider of it into rational animal (which is human) and non-rational animal (which is not human). He said 'and the muqawwim of the higher': like 'growing' (nami) which is a constituent of the growing body (al-jism al-nami) which is the tree and so on, is a constituent of the lower which is animal and human as well. For animal and human share in body with other bodies, so when the growing body is distinguished from other kinds of bodies by 'growing', then animal and human are also distinguished from other kinds of bodies by being growing, because the growing body is a part of animal and human. So the distinguishing mark that is its portion is also the portion of what is composed of it, and animal and human are among that which is composed of it.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive definition of the differentia (fasl) and then explains its two fundamental aspects: being constitutive (muqawwim) and being divisive (muqassim). It begins linguistically: 'fasl' means cutting, then used for that by which a thing is distinguished from another, and finally logicians restricted it to the essential differentiator. Next, the passage explains that the differentia relates to two things: to the quiddity it distinguishes (making it a part and therefore 'muqawwim') and to the genus from which it distinguishes that quiddity (making it a divider of the genus, 'muqassim'). An example is given: 'rational' divides animal into rational (human) and non-rational. The passage then discusses the principle that a differentia which is a constituent of a higher genus/species is also a constituent of the lower because the higher is part of the lower. It clarifies the terms 'higher' and 'lower' to include intermediate levels. Finally, it provides a concrete example: 'growing' (nami) is a differentia for growing body, and since animal and human have growing body as a part, they are also distinguished by it from non-growing bodies. The commentary stresses the dual function of the differentia as both a building block of the species and a tool for dividing the genus.

الفصل
القطع
الذاتي
المطلق
المقيد

B) They restricted it to essential differentiators.
C) They expanded it to include accidents.

Key Takeaway
The differentia in logic is not just any distinction; it is an essential attribute that constitutes the species.

The Two Aspects of Fasl: Muqawwim and Muqassim
Author explains the two considerations of fasl: as constitutive part and as divisor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two relations of the differentia (muqawwim and muqassim) and apply them to examples from Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
The same differentia both constitutes the species and divides the genus.

Once we understand that fasl is the essential differentiator, we must appreciate its dual role. It is not merely a part of the species; it also functions as a tool to split the genus into its subcategories. This lesson explores how the same attribute (e.g., 'rational') plays both roles depending on what it is related to.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two relations
The differentia relates to the quiddity it distinguishes and to the genus from which it distinguishes. When related to the species, it is a part of its essence (muqawwim). When related to the genus, it divides the genus (muqassim).
2
Analyse the example of 'natiq'
'Rational' is muqawwim for human and muqassim for animal. For human, rationality is an essential part; for animal, rationality splits the genus animal into rational and non-rational.
3
Examine the inheritance principle
The muqawwim of the higher is muqawwim of the lower. If a differentia constitutes a higher genus, it also constitutes any lower species that includes that genus as a part.
The passage provides a logical argument for this, which we will formalize.
4
Apply to a concrete Islamic example
Use 'hayah' (life) as a differentia for living body. Life constitutes the living body, and it also divides 'body' into living and non-living. Then for animal, life is still constitutive because animal includes living body.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The passage then discusses the principle that a differentia which is a constituent of a higher genus/species is also a constituent of the lower because the higher is part of the lower. It clarifies the terms 'higher' and 'lower' to include intermediate levels. Finally, it provides a concrete example: 'growing' (nami) is a differentia for growing body, and since animal and human have growing body as a part, they are also distinguished by it from non-growing bodies. The commentary stresses the dual function of the differentia as both a building block of the species and a tool for dividing the genus.

Rule on Inferior and Superior: Differentia and Division
Commentary on the rule that the differentia of the inferior does not apply to the superior, but division of the inferior applies to the superior.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule regarding the asymmetry of differentia and division between superior and inferior universals to validate definitions and classifications in Islamic logic.

Core Idea
The differentia of the species does not ascend to the genus, but the division of the species does divide the genus.

In the study of the five universals, knowing how genus and species relate is essential. A common mistake is to assume that what distinguishes a species also distinguishes its genus. This lesson clarifies that the differentia of the inferior (species) does not apply to the superior (genus), while the division of the inferior necessarily applies to the superior. We will analyze the reasoning behind this rule using the example of 'rational' as a differentia of man but not of animal.

Guided Path
1
Restate the Rule
Identify the two parts of the rule from the passage: 'لا عكس' means that the differentia of the inferior is not a differentia of the superior; 'والمقسم بالعكس' means that the division of the inferior is a division of the superior.
2
Apply to an Example: Differentia
Consider 'animal' (superior) and 'man' (inferior). 'Rational' is a differentia of man. Check if 'rational' is also a differentia of animal. It is not, because animal includes both rational and non-rational beings. Hence, the differentia does not transfer upward.
This illustrates the first part of the rule.
3
Apply to an Example: Division
Now, man divides into rational and non-rational. Does this division also apply to animal? Yes, because animal includes both rational and non-rational individuals. So the division of the species applies to the genus.
This illustrates the second part of the rule.
4
Understand the Reasoning
The differentia of a species is a distinctive attribute that narrows the genus; it cannot apply to the broader genus because the genus lacks that distinction uniformly. However, the division of the species is based on a property that exists within the genus, since the species is a subset. Therefore, any division of the species corresponds to a division within the genus.
The passage provides a metaphysical explanation: the features of the inferior shrink its scope and cannot ascend, while the superior's constitutives can descend.
5
Test Your Understanding with a New Example
Given the genus 'substance' (جوهر) and species 'body' (جسم), is the differentia of body (e.g., having three dimensions) a differentia of substance? No. But does the division of body into 'living' and 'non-living' apply to substance? Yes, because substance includes both living and non-living bodies.
This confirms the rule with an Islamic kalam example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

للسافل مقسم للعالى نفسه. قوله ولا عكس: أي مقوم السافل لا يكون مقوماً للعالى لأن السافل لا يترقى إلى العالي حتى يكسبه مميزاته وخصوصياته، بخلاف العالي فإن العالي إذا قيد بقيود وخصص بمخصصات نزع عن نفسه عنوان العلو والعموم وصار هو السافل عيناً، والسافل يمكنه بعد حذف مخصصاته وقيوده أن يصير عالياً ولكنه خلاف مفروض البحث هنا، فإن المميزات إذا لحقت الحقيقة صغرتها عن نفسها قبل لحوقها بها، الحيوان قبل أن يلحقه مائز الناطق كان أوسع دائرة من نفسه عند ما لحقه هذا المائز، فمن هنا تبين أن مميزات السافل لا تسري إلى العالي لأن سراية السافل إلى العالي محتاجة إلى أن يحذف السافل عن المميزات التي تبعده عن العالي وتصغر دائرته بالنسبة إلى عمومه وانتساب المقومات إلى السافل يربطه إلى مكانه البعيد عن العالي وبين حذف المميزات ولحوقها تمانع، فكيف تسري مقومات السافل إلى العالي؟ وأما مقومات العالي فإنها تنزل به درجة درجة فهي تقربه إلى السافل فضلاً عن كون العالي جزءاً للسافل دخيلاً في مقام ذاته فهو يمده بجوهريته، والسافل ليس جزءاً للعالي حتى يمده من هذا الطريق بجوهريته وخصائصه الذاتية، ولا عين العالي ولا مثل العالي، فليست من طريق السافل مندوحة يتوصل بها إلى العالي حتى يوصله شيئاً من مميزاته الذاتية. قوله والمقسم بالعكس أي أن ما يقسم السافل بالملازمة يقسم العالي، لأن السافل وهو الحيوان مثلاً إذا انقسم إلى ناطق وغير ناطق فقد أوجب الحيوان نفسه أن ينقسم النامي إلى ناطق وغير ناطق لأن النامي جزءه والحقيقة الملتئمة من أجزاء إذا انشطرت انشطرت معها أجزاؤها إذ ليست وراء الأجزاء شيئاً. وأما ما يقسم العالي فلا يقسم السافل لأن العالي الذي يكون جزءاً للسافل هو العالي من حيث هو لا بما له من خصوصيات وتشعبات، لأنه إذا روعيت هذه التشعبات والخصوصيات فيه لا يكون بإطلاقه جزء بل بشعبة منه بحيث تلائم هذا السافل، وأما الإطلاق على أرساله في الشعب والخصوصيات فهو مباين له لا جزء منه، مثلاً الجسم الذي هو جزء في الجسم النامي هو الجسم من حيث هو مغضوضاً عن كونه جماداً ونباتاً وحيواناً، فإن هذه الخصوصيات إذا روعيت فيه لم يكن جزءاً للنامي إلا من شعبة النباتية أو الحيوانية لا مطلقاً، فلذا لا ينحفظ ارتباط العالي بالسافل إلا مع غض النظر عن خصوصياته التي تشطره وتشعبه، ومع غض النظر عنها كيف تسري إلى السافل؟ إذن فتقسيمات العالي مع مراعاة حفظ ارتباطه بالسافل وأنه جزء منه واجبة الإغفال، وإذا أغفلت فليست تسري، فاعرفه حق معرفته.
And not the converse, and the division by the converse. His statement 'and not the converse' means universally, that is, not every constitutive element of the inferior is constitutive of the superior; for example, 'rational' is constitutive of the inferior which is man, but it is not constitutive of the superior which is animal. His statement 'and the division by the converse' means: every divisor of the inferior is a divisor of the superior itself. His statement 'and not the converse': that is, the constitutive element of the inferior cannot be constitutive of the superior because the inferior does not ascend to the superior such that it would acquire its distinguishing features and particularities, unlike the superior; for the superior, when it is restricted by restrictions and specified by specifications, strips itself of the title of superiority and generality and becomes the inferior itself; and the inferior, after removing its specifications and restrictions, can become superior, but that is contrary to the assumed subject of inquiry here. For when distinguishing features attach to a reality, they shrink it from what it was before their attachment; for example, animal before being joined by the differentia 'rational' had a wider scope than itself when this differentia joined it. From this it becomes clear that the distinguishing features of the inferior do not extend to the superior, because the extension of the inferior to the superior requires that the inferior be stripped of the distinguishing features that distance it from the superior and shrink its scope relative to its generality; and the attribution of the constitutives to the inferior ties it to its remote place from the superior, and there is a mutual opposition between removing the features and their attachment, so how can the constitutives of the inferior extend to the superior? As for the constitutives of the superior, they descend with it degree by degree, thus bringing it closer to the inferior, in addition to the superior being a part of the inferior, entering into the station of its essence; so it supplies it with its quiddity, while the inferior is not a part of the superior such that it would supply it through this path with its quiddity and essential properties; neither the essence of the superior nor the example of the superior, so there is no escape from the path of the inferior to reach the superior such that it would convey to it something of its essential distinguishing features. His statement 'and the division by the converse' means that what divides the inferior by implication divides the superior, because if the inferior, which is animal for example, divides into rational and non-rational, then animal itself necessitates that the growing body (al-nami) divides into rational and non-rational, because the growing body is its part, and a reality composed of parts, when it splits, its parts split with it, since there is nothing beyond the parts. As for what divides the superior, it does not divide the inferior, because the superior that is a part of the inferior is the superior insofar as it is, not with its particularities and ramifications; because if these ramifications and particularities are taken into account in it, it is not absolutely a part but a branch of it that suits this inferior; and the absolute release in branches and particularities is incompatible with it, not a part of it. For example, body, which is a part of the growing body, is body insofar as it is, overlooking its being inanimate, plant, or animal; for if these particularities are taken into account in it, it is not a part of the growing body except from the branch of plant or animal, not absolutely. Therefore, the connection of the superior to the inferior is not preserved except by disregarding its particularities that split and branch it; and with disregard for them, how can it extend to the inferior? Thus, the divisions of the superior, while observing the preservation of its connection to the inferior and that it is a part of it, are necessarily to be overlooked, and if overlooked, they do not extend. Know this well.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rule 'لا عكس والمقسم بالعكس' (not the converse, and the division by the converse) from the matn. The commentator explains two principles regarding the relationship between a superior universal (like genus) and an inferior universal (like species). First, the differentia (fصل) of the inferior does not become a differentia for the superior. For example, 'rational' distinguishes man (inferior) but not animal (superior), because the inferior is a subset and its distinguishing features are specific to it; they do not ascend to the broader superior. The commentator illustrates with animal and man: animal without the differentia 'rational' has a wider scope than when it is specified by that differentia. The distinctive features of the inferior shrink its scope, so they cannot be applied to the superior which is more general. The superior, when restricted, becomes the inferior, but the inferior's features do not transfer upward. The commentator also notes that the constitutive elements of the superior can descend into the inferior because the superior is part of the inferior's essence, but not vice versa. Second, the opposite principle holds: any division of the inferior is also a division of the superior. For instance, if animal divides into rational and non-rational, then the growing body (a higher genus containing animal) must also divide into rational and non-rational because animal is a part of it. The division of a composite reality entails the division of its parts. However, the division of the superior does not necessarily divide the inferior, because the superior as part of the inferior is considered only in its absolute nature, disregarding its specific branches. For example, body as part of a growing body is body without being specified as inanimate, plant, or animal. If those specifications are added, it becomes a branch, not the absolute part that fits the inferior. Therefore, to maintain the connection, we must overlook the superior's internal divisions, so they do not extend downward. This discussion reinforces the proper application of the five universals in definition and division within Islamic logic.

Key Terms
مقوم (muqawwim): A constitutive element that enters into the essence of something, such as the differentia for a species or the genus for a species.
سافل (sāfil): The inferior universal, i.e., the more specific term like species (e.g., man) in contrast to the superior genus (e.g., animal).
عالى (ʿālī): The superior universal, i.e., the more general term like genus (e.g., animal) in contrast to the inferior species.
عكس (ʿaks): Conversion; here it means the reciprocal relationship in the context of constitutive elements and division between superior and inferior. [Note: In standard logic, 'aks usually refers to conversion of propositions; here it is used in a technical sense about universals.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) None of the above.

Key Takeaway
The differentia of a species is unique to it and does not extend to its genus, but any division of the species necessarily divides the genus.

Proprium and Common Accident: Definitions and Subdivisions
Author defines proprium and common accident with subdivisions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish proprium from common accident and identify their subdivisions (evident/non-evident concomitant, inclusive/exclusive, species/genus).

Core Idea
Proprium is exclusive but accidental; common accident is shared and accidental.

In this passage, the author defines the fourth and fifth of the five universals: the proprium (khassa) and the common accident ('arad 'amm). These are both accidental predicates, but the key difference is scope: the proprium applies exclusively to one quiddity, while the common accident applies to multiple. The author also introduces subdivisions such as necessary concomitant (lazim) and distinguishes proprium based on inclusivity and type of quiddity. By mastering these distinctions, you will be able to correctly classify predicates in Islamic sciences like fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate where the author defines proprium and common accident. Proprium is 'the external predicated of what falls under a single quiddity'; common accident is 'the external predicated of it and of other things.'
The key difference is exclusivity of predication.
2
Understand 'external' (kharij)
The author explains that 'external' means the predicate is not part of the essence (quiddity). Both proprium and common accident are accidental, not essential.
This distinguishes them from genus and differentia.
3
Analyze the subdivision of necessary concomitant (lazim)
If a proprium or common accident is inseparable from the subject, it is a necessary concomitant. It can be evident (conception follows directly from the subject) or non-evident.
Example: 'laughter' is a necessary concomitant of man, but not all proprium are necessary.
4
Explore further subdivisions of proprium
The proprium divides into inclusive (applies to all individuals, e.g., 'potential writer') and non-inclusive (applies to some, e.g., 'actual writer'). It also divides by quiddity type: species-specific (e.g., 'laughter' for man) or genus-specific (e.g., 'walker' for animal).
A proprium for a genus can be a common accident for a species under it.
5
Apply the conversion rule
The author states that the division of the superior does not convert to the inferior. For example, 'sensitive' divides 'growing body' (superior) but not 'animal' (inferior). This illustrates how predicates apply across levels.
This rule helps avoid misclassifying predicates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع: الخاصة وهو الخارج المقول على ما تحت حقيقة واحدة الخامس: العرض العام وهو الخارج المقول عليها وعلى غيرها. وكل منهما إن امتنع انفكاكه عن الشيء فلازم بالنظر إلى الماهية أو الوجود، بيّن يلزم تصوره من تصور الملزوم أو من تصورهما والنسبة بينهما الجزم باللزوم وغير بيّن. ولا عكس أي كلياً. أما الأول: فلأن السافل قسم من العالي فكل فصل حصل للسافل قسماً فقد حصل للعالي قسماً لأن قسم القسم قسم. وأما الثاني: فلأن الحساس مثلاً مقسم للعالي الذي هو الجسم النامي وليس مقسماً للسافل الذي هو الحيوان. قوله وهو الخارج: أي الكلي الخارج، فإن المقسم معتبر في جميع مفهومات الأقسام. واعلم أن الخاصة تنقسم إلى خاصة شاملة لجميع أفراد ما هي خاصة له كالكاتب بالقوة للإنسان، وإلى غير شاملة لجميع أفراد ما هي خاصة له كالكاتب بالفعل له. قوله حقيقة واحدة: نوعية أو جنسية، فالأول خاصة النوع كالضاحك، والثاني خاصة الجنس كالماشي، فالماشي خاصة للحيوان وعرض عام للإنسان فافهم. قوله وعلى غيرها كالماشي يقال على حقيقة الإنسان وعلى غيرها من الحقائق الحيوانية. قوله وكل منها أي كل من الخاصة والعرض العام. وبالجملة الكلي الخارج المقول على ما تحت حقيقة واحدة هو الخاصة، والمقول على ما تحتها وعلى غيرها هو العرض العام.
The fourth: the proprium (al-khassa), which is the external [predicate] predicated of what falls under a single quiddity. The fifth: the common accident (al-'arad al-'amm), which is the external [predicate] predicated of it and of other things. And each of them, if its separation from the thing is impossible, then it is a necessary concomitant with respect to quiddity or existence; [it is] evident if its conception follows from the conception of the thing accompanied, or from the conception of both and the relation between them [is] the judgment of concomitance, and [if] not evident. And no conversion, i.e., universally. As for the first: because the inferior is a part of the superior, so every differentia that becomes a part for the inferior has become a part for the superior, because the part of a part is a part. As for the second: because 'sensitive' (al-hassas), for example, is a divisor of the superior which is the growing body (al-jism al-nami), but is not a divisor of the inferior which is animal. His statement 'and it is the external': i.e., the external universal, for the divisor is considered in all concepts of the divisions. Know that the proprium divides into a proprium inclusive of all individuals of what it is a proprium for, such as 'writer in potentia' for man, and into one not inclusive of all individuals of what it is a proprium for, such as 'writer in act' for him. His statement 'a single quiddity': specific or generic; the first is a proprium of the species like 'laughter', and the second is a proprium of the genus like 'walker'; so 'walker' is a proprium for animal and a common accident for man; understand. His statement 'and of other things': like 'walker' is said of the quiddity of man and of other animal quiddities. His statement 'and each of them': i.e., each of the proprium and the common accident. In summary, the external universal predicated of what is under a single quiddity is the proprium, and predicated of what is under it and of others is the common accident.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth and fifth of the five universals: the proprium (special characteristic) and the common accident. The author begins by stating that the proprium is a non-essential predicate that applies only to a single quiddity (e.g., 'capable of writing' for man), while the common accident applies to that quiddity and to others (e.g., 'walking' applies to man, horse, etc.). Then a clarification: if either of these is inseparable from the subject, it is called a necessary concomitant (lazim), which may be evident (if its conception follows directly from the subject) or non-evident. Next, a note on conversion ('aks): the rule that the differentia of the inferior does not apply to the superior, but the division does, is reiterated. The author then explains that the proprium can be inclusive (e.g., potential writer for all humans) or non-inclusive (e.g., actual writer only for some). Finally, the proprium is further divided based on whether the quiddity is a species (e.g., 'laughter' specific to man) or a genus (e.g., 'walker' specific to animal but common to man). The common accident is then clarified as being predicated of multiple quiddities. The commentary reinforces the definitions with examples from the Islamic sciences: for instance, 'laughter' is a proprium of man (since only man laughs), while 'walking' is a common accident because it applies to man and other animals.

The proprium is an exclusive but accidental universal; the common accident is a shared accidental universal; both are external predicates.

Definition of Khassa and 'Arad 'Amm
Defining the fourth and fifth universals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the fourth universal (khassa) from the fifth ('arad 'amm) based on their scope of application and identify examples of each.

Core Idea
Khassa applies to one reality; 'Arad 'Amm applies to multiple realities.

The fourth and fifth universals are both accidental predicates, but they differ in scope. Understanding this distinction is essential for proper definition and classification in logic. The passage defines them clearly with examples from the Islamic logical tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the Arabic terms being defined: الخاصة (khassa) and العرض العام ('arad 'amm). Note their positions as the fourth and fifth in the list of five universals.
The passage begins with 'The fourth: special property' and 'The fifth: common accident'.
2
Extract the genus
Both are introduced as 'external predicate' (الخارج المقول). This means they are accidental, not part of the essence. Understand what 'external' excludes: the three essential predicates (genus, species, differentia).
The commentator explains: 'Excluded by external are the three essential predicates'.
3
Distinguish the differentia
Khassa is 'said of what is under one reality' (على ما تحت حقيقة واحدة). 'Arad 'amm is 'said of that reality and on others' (علىها وعلى غيرها). Compare the scope: khassa applies to all individuals of a single kind; 'arad 'amm applies to multiple kinds.
Example: 'laughing' is khassa for man; 'walking' is 'arad 'amm for man because it also applies to horse.
4
Test with examples
Apply the definitions to new examples from Islamic sciences. For instance, is 'sleeping' khassa or 'arad 'amm for man? Since animals also sleep, it is 'arad 'amm. Is 'rational' khassa? But rational is differentia, not accidental, so excluded by 'external'.
This step reinforces the distinction between essential and accidental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع: الخاصة و هو الخارج المقول (٥) على ما تحت حقيقة واحدة الخامس: العرض العام وهو الخارج المقول عليها وعلى غيرها . و كل منهما ان امتنع انفكاكه عن الشيء فلازم بالنظر الى الماهية او الوجود، بيّن يلزم تصوره من تصور الملزوم او من تصور هما و النسبة بينهما الجزم باللزوم و غير بين ولا عکسی (۱۲۰) اما الاول: فلان السافل قسم من العالى فكل فصل حصل للسافل قسماً فقد حصل للعالى قسماً لان قسم القسم قسم . (۱۲۱) و اما الثاني فلان الحساس مثلاً مقسم للعالى الذي هو الجسم النامي وليس مقسماً للسائل الذي هو الحيوان (۱۲۲) . قوله «وهو الخارج»: اى الكلى الخارج، فان المقسم معتبر في جميع مفهومات الاقسام و اعلم ان الخاصة (۱۲۳) تنقسم الى خاصة شاملة لجميع افراد ما هي خاصة له كالكاتب بالقوه للانسان والى غير شاملة لجميع افراد ما هي خاصة له كالكاتب بالفعل له . قوله « حقيقة واحدة»: نوعية او جنسية (۱۲۴) فالاول خاصة النوع كالضاحك (۱۲۵) و الثانى خاصة الجنس كالماشي فالماشى خاصة للحيوان وعرض عام للانسان فاقهم . (١٢٦) قوله و على غيرها كالماشى يقال على حقيقة الانسان و على غيرها من الحقائق الحيوانية. قوله وكل منها اى كل من الخاصة والعرض المعام. وبالجملة الكلى (٥) قول المصنف الخاصة وهو الخارج المقول الخارج المقول ... خرج بالخارج الذاتيات الثلاثة و بالقيد الاخيرا عنى قوله «فقط» العرض العام ، لانه كما سيجيء لا يختص بافراد حقيقة واحدة والقاء في الخاصة للنقل من الوصفية وذلك لان اللفظ اذا نقل من الوصفية الى الاسمية لغلبة الاستعمال كان اسميته فرعاً لوصفيته فاشبه المؤثث فى ان فى كل واحد منها فرعية اذ المؤنث فرع المذكر فادخل عليه التاء دلالة على ذلك كما ادخلت على المؤنث
The fourth: special property (khassa), and it is the external predicate said of what is under one reality. The fifth: common accident ('arad 'amm), and it is the external predicate said of that reality and of others. And each of them, if its disjunction from the thing is impossible, then it is necessary (lazim) with respect to essence or existence; bayyin (clear) in that its conception follows from the conception of the subject, or from the conception of both and the relation between them there is certainty of implication; and non-bayyin. And there is no conversion for both... As for the first: because the lower is a division of the higher, so every differentia that makes the lower a division has made the higher a division, for the division of a division is a division. As for the second: because 'sensitive' for example is a divider for the higher which is the growing body, and it is not a divider for the lower which is the animal. His saying: 'and it is the external': meaning the external universal, for the divider is considered in all concepts of the divisions. Know that the special property (khassa) is divided into a special property that includes all individuals of that for which it is special, like the potential writer for man, and one that does not include all individuals of that for which it is special, like the actual writer for him. His saying: 'one reality': specific or generic. So the first is a special property of the species like 'laughing', and the second is a special property of the genus like 'walking'. So 'walking' is a special property for animal and a common accident for man, so understand. His saying: 'and on others' like 'walking' is said of the reality of man and of other animal realities. His saying: 'and each of them' i.e. each of the special property and the common accident. In summary, the universal... (5) The saying of the author: 'the special property and it is the external predicate, the external predicate...' Excluded by 'external' are the three essential predicates, and by the last restriction, i.e. his saying 'only', the common accident, because as will come, it is not restricted to individuals of one reality. The feminine ending in 'khassa' is due to transference from adjective to noun, for when a word is transferred from adjective to noun due to frequent usage, its noun status is derivative of its adjective status, so it resembles the feminine in that each of them is derivative, since the feminine is derivative from the masculine, so the ta was inserted to indicate that, just as it was inserted in the feminine.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a definitional commentary on the fourth and fifth universals (al-khassa and al-'arad al-'amm) from the Isaghuji tradition. The author first gives the definitions: special property (khassa) is the external predicate that applies to individuals under a single reality (e.g., 'laughing' for man), while common accident ('arad 'amm) is the external predicate that applies to that reality and to others (e.g., 'walking' applies to both man and horse). He then notes that each of these, if inseparable (imtana'a infikakuhu), is called 'necessary' (lazim) with respect to essence or existence. Next, he discusses 'clear' (bayyin) vs. 'non-clear' (ghayr bayyin) as well as the impossibility of conversion for both. The hashiya explains the author's statement 'and it is the external' by clarifying that it means the universal that is external to the quiddity (i.e., not essential). The divider (muqassim) is included in all concepts of the divisions. He then divides khassa into two types: one that covers all individuals (like potential writing for man) and one that does not (like actual writing). He explains that 'one reality' can be specific (species) or generic (genus), giving examples: laughing (specific to man) and walking (specific to animal, common accident for man). The passage also includes a grammatical note about why 'khassa' takes the feminine ta, attributing it to transference from adjective to noun, analogous to feminine derivation.

Key Terms
الخاصة
العرض العام
الخارج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of a special property (khassa) of the species 'man'?
A) 'Walking' (al-mashi)
B) 'Laughing' (al-dahik)
C) 'Animal' (al-hayawan)
D) 'Body' (al-jism)

Key Takeaway
Khassa is restricted to one reality, while 'arad 'amm spans multiple realities; both are external (accidental) predicates.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given the following predicates, classify each as khassa or 'arad 'amm for the species 'man': 'speaking', 'walking', 'laughing', 'writing'. Use the definitions from the passage.
?
Provide a definition of 'horse' and identify which universals (genus, species, differentia, khassa, 'arad 'amm) appear in it.

Division of Khassa into Inclusive and Non-Inclusive
Dividing special property into inclusive and non-inclusive

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a special property that covers all individuals of a species (inclusive) and one that does not (non-inclusive), using the examples of potential and actual writer.

Core Idea
A special property may be potential (covering all) or actual (not covering all).

The passage divides khassa into two types based on whether it applies to every individual of the species or only some. This division is important for precision in definitions, especially when dealing with dispositions versus actual occurrences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the division
Locate where the text says 'اعلم ان الخاصة تنقسم الى خاصة شاملة... والى غير شاملة'. Note that khassa is divided into two categories.
The text uses 'كاتب بالقوة' (potential writer) and 'كاتب بالفعل' (actual writer).
2
Understand 'shamil' (inclusive)
A 'shamil' khassa applies to every individual of the species. Example: 'potential writer' applies to all humans, as all humans have the potential to write (with education).
Potentiality is a constant attribute of the species.
3
Understand 'ghayr shamil' (non-inclusive)
A non-inclusive khassa applies only to some individuals of the species. Example: 'actual writer' applies only to those who have actually written.
Actuality is not a permanent attribute of all individuals.
4
Apply to other examples
Think of other attributes: 'laughing' is a potential property of all humans (the capacity to laugh), but 'actually laughing' is not always present. Which type of khassa is 'laughing' generally considered? The passage earlier treated 'laughing' as khassa without specifying, but here we see the nuance.
This division clarifies how a single property can be considered in different ways.

6 min
Lazim and Bayyin Accidents
Explaining necessary and self-evident accidents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether an accidental property is lazim (inseparable) and whether it is bayyin (self-evident) based on the conditions given in the passage.

Core Idea
Some accidents are inseparable and self-evident; their conception follows from the subject.

The passage discusses a further division of accidents (including khassa and 'arad 'amm) into necessary (lazim) and non-necessary, and among necessary, into clear (bayyin) and unclear. This helps in understanding which properties are logically entailed by the subject's essence.

Guided Path
1
Understand the condition for lazim
An accident is lazim if its separation from the thing is impossible (امتنع انفكاكه عن الشيء). This impossibility can be with respect to essence (ماهية) or existence (وجود).
For example, 'existence' is lazim for the Necessary Being, but for contingent beings, existence is not lazim.
2
Identify the two types of bayyin
A bayyin accident is one where its conception follows from the subject alone (من تصور الملزوم) or from the subject, the accident, and the relation (من تصور هما والنسبة). The first is 'bayyin ma'na akhass' and the second 'bayyin ma'na a'amm'.
The passage says 'يلزم تصوره من تصور الملزوم' for the first, and for the second 'من تصور هما والنسبة بينهما الجزم باللزوم'.
3
Distinguish from non-bayyin
If neither condition holds, the accident is 'ghayr bayyin' (non-clear). The passage also notes that there is no conversion for both types (ولا عکسی).
Conversion is another logical operation not detailed here.
4
Apply to examples from Kalam
Given an accident like 'contingency' for the world, is it lazim? Yes, the world is inherently contingent. Is it bayyin? The conception of contingency follows from the conception of the world as temporally originated, so it is bayyin.
Use the example from the passage: 'sensitive' for growing body is bayyin because the concept of sensitivity follows from the concept of growing body?
